Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
8 min
Innate Religiosity and Moral Discernment
Author presents innate religiosity and moral discernment as manifestations of fitra.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the evidence the author provides for innate religiosity and moral discernment as part of fitra.

Core Idea
Humans are naturally disposed to worship and have an innate sense of moral good and evil.

This lesson continues the exploration of fitra, focusing on two additional manifestations: innate religiosity (al-taʿabbud) and the innate moral sense that distinguishes good from evil. The author provides historical and experiential evidence, including a Qur'anic verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about worship
The author states that worship is a fixed manifestation of fitra throughout history. Find the sentence that says this.
2
Examine the evidence
The author offers three pieces of evidence: 1) The universality of religion across time and place. 2) The presence of places of worship everywhere. 3) The instinctual turning to God during hardships, even by atheists. Note the Qur'anic verse (29:65) as support.
3
Consider the moral discernment
The author lists another manifestation: the soul naturally distinguishes high from low, prefers the noble over the base, and works to elevate truthfulness and honesty while lowering falsehood and betrayal. This shows an innate moral sense.
4
Synthesize the manifestations
Reflect on how these manifestations—worship and moral sense—are part of human nature. They cannot be changed or eliminated.

Source Text

ويقال لمن يمارس هذا النوع من الجنس بانه شاذ عن القاعدة الفطرية ويقال الكلام نفسه لمن يمارس الجنس مع مثيله ومن أمثلة القوانين الفطرية غريزة السعي للبقاء ورفض الموت والفناء كراهة النقص والعشق للكمال المطلق و الجمال المحض (فقد جبل جميع البشر من غير استثناء على العشق للكمال فمع التجول في الأدوار التي مرت بها البشرية واستنطاق كل فرد من أفرادهم وكل طائفة من طوائفهم نجد أن هذا العشق و الحب قد جبل في طينته ونجد أن قلبه متوجه نحو الكمال بل جميع حركاته ومساعيه ليست هي إلا لأجل هذا الحب الكامن في ضميره فهو يريد الوصول إلى الكمال ويطلب مشاهدة معشوقه ومحبوبه وكل يجد معشوقه في شيء فيطلب ذلك الشيء و يتفانى في سبيله فأهل الدنيا يحسبون الكمال في الثروة فيسعون للوصول إليها وأهل العلم في العلم وأهل الآخرة في العبادة وهكذا فالناس جميعهم يسعون نحو الكمال فإذا تصوروه في موجود أو موهوم تعلقوا به وعشقوه ولكن على الرغم من ذلك فليس عشقهم لهذا الذي ظنوه بأنه معشوقهم وهذا الذي توهموه وتخيلوه ليس هو كعبة آمالهم إذ لو رجع الإنسان إلى فطرته لوجد أن قلبه في الوقت الذي يُظهر العشق لشيء ما فإنه يتحول عن هذا المعشوق إلى غيره إذا وجد الثاني أكمل من الأول وهكذا بل إن نيران عشقه لتزداد اشتعالاً فالإنسان يحب الجمال فيصل إليه ولا يقتنع به بل يطلب أجمل منه وهكذا و يعشق القدرة فيصل إليها ثم لا يستقر بل يتزايد حبه إليها ولا تخمد نار اشتياقه أصلاً بل تزداد لهيباً وهذه الحالة تشمل جميع افراد البشرية من غير استثناء. ثم إن الإنسان إنما يعشق الكمال الذي لا عيب فيه ولا كمال بعده والعلم الذي لا جهل فيه والقدرة التي لاعجز فيها والحياة التي لاموت فيها أي الكمال المطلق) ومن مظاهر الفطرة الثابتة الى مدار التاريخ التعبد وهذه حقيقة غير قابلة للتبديل أو التغيير فالإنسان قد خلق وخلق معه الإحساس بالحاجة إلى الركون إلى عقيدة ما والتاريخ يشهد ويؤكد على أن ما من عصر أو زمان أو مكان إلا وكان الناس فيه متدينون بدين ونحن اليوم نجد في كل مدينة أو قرية مركزاً للعبادة سواء كان هذا المركز معبداً للأوثان أو كنيسةً أو مسجداً ثم ( إن الإنسان مفطور على اللجوء إلى ربـه تبارك وتعالى عنـد الشدائد فإذا ما وقع الإنسان أي إنسان حتى الكافر الملحد في شدة أو أحدق به خطر فإن الخيالات والأوهام تتطاير من ذهنه ويبقى ما فطر عليه ليصيح بأعلى صوته ومن قرارة نفسه وعميق قلبه منادياً ربه؛ ليفرج كربته وهمه ويلجأ إليه وحده دون سواه) وصدق الله تعالى إذ يقول (فَإِذَا رَكَبُوا فِي الْفُلْكِ دَعَوْا اللهَ مُخْلِصِينَ لَهُ الدِّينَ فَلَمَّا نَجَاهُمْ إِلَى الْبَرِّ إِذَا هُمْ يُشْرِكُونَ) ومن مظاهر الفطرة ان النفس الإنسانية لا تساوي بين العالي والسافل والشريف والوضيع فإن من طبعها التفريق بينهما وتفضيل العالي والشريف والخير على السافل والوضيع والشرير وتنفر غاية النفور من ترفع الأراذل وخفض الأفاضل، إن النفس تعمل على اعلاء قيم الصدق والامانة وإسفال قيم الكذب والخيانة وترى العدل كل العدل أن ينزل كل شيء منزلته ومن مظاهر الفطرة ان الانسان يقبل الخير حين يعلم بأنه خير ويرفض الشر حين يعلم بأنه شر ومن مصاديق الفطرة عشق الراحة وعشق الحرية
And it is said to whoever practices this type of sexuality that he is deviant from the innate norm, and the same is said to whoever practices homosexuality. And among the examples of innate laws are the instinct to seek survival and reject death and annihilation, hatred of deficiency, and love of absolute perfection and pure beauty. (Indeed, all humans without exception have been created with a love for perfection. So as we go through the stages humanity has passed and interrogate every individual and every group, we find that this love and affection has been ingrained in their nature, and we find that their heart is directed towards perfection. Rather, all their movements and efforts are only for the sake of this love hidden in their conscience. They want to reach perfection and seek to see their beloved. Everyone finds their beloved in something, so they seek that thing and sacrifice themselves for it. The worldly people think perfection is in wealth, so they strive to attain it; the people of knowledge in knowledge; the people of the Hereafter in worship; and so on. All people strive towards perfection. So when they conceive it in something existent or imagined, they attach themselves to it and love it. But despite that, their love for what they thought was their beloved and what they imagined and supposed is not the Kaaba of their hopes. For if a person returns to his innate nature, he finds that his heart, while showing love for something, turns away from that beloved to another if he finds the second more perfect than the first, and so on. Rather, the fires of his love increase in intensity. Man loves beauty and attains it, but is not satisfied; he seeks something more beautiful, and so on. He loves power and attains it, then does not settle; rather, his love for it increases, and the fire of his longing is not extinguished at all; rather, it increases in flames. This state includes all human beings without exception. Then man only loves perfection that has no defect and beyond which there is no perfection, knowledge that has no ignorance in it, power that has no inability, life that has no death—that is, absolute perfection.) And among the fixed manifestations of fitra throughout history is worship. This is a fact that cannot be altered or changed. Man was created, and with him was created the feeling of need to rely on some creed. History witnesses and confirms that there is no age, time, or place where people were not religious with a religion. Today we find in every city or village a center of worship, whether that center is a temple of idols, a church, or a mosque. Then (man is innately disposed to turn to his Lord, Blessed and Exalted, during hardships. For if a person—any person, even a disbelieving atheist—falls into hardship or danger closes in on him, the fantasies and illusions fly from his mind, and what he was created upon remains for him to cry out at the top of his voice, from the bottom of his soul and the depth of his heart, calling upon his Lord to relieve his distress and worry, and he takes refuge in Him alone without others.) And God Almighty speaks truth when He says: (And when they board the ship, they supplicate Allah, sincere to Him in religion, but when He delivers them to the land, at once they associate others with Him.) And among the manifestations of fitra is that the human soul does not equate the high and the low, the noble and the base. For it is its nature to differentiate between them and to prefer the high, the noble, and the good over the low, the base, and the evil, and it is extremely repulsed by the elevation of the vile and the debasement of the virtuous. The soul works to elevate the values of truthfulness and honesty and to lower the values of lying and betrayal. It sees that complete justice is to place everything in its proper position. And among the manifestations of fitra is that man accepts good when he knows it is good and rejects evil when he knows it is evil. And among the instances of fitra are love of comfort and love of freedom.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the manifestations of innate human nature (fitra), a key epistemological concept in Islamic thought. The author begins by referencing deviant sexual practices as violations of fitra, then enumerates several innate inclinations. First is the instinct for self-preservation and aversion to death and deficiency. Central is the innate love (ʿishq) for absolute perfection and pure beauty. The author argues that all humans are created with this love; it is the hidden driver behind all pursuits—wealth, knowledge, worship, etc. However, the beloved objects are never fully satisfying; as humans attain one object, they soon seek a more perfect one, demonstrating that the true beloved is absolute perfection without any defect. The second major manifestation is innate religiosity (taʿabbud): humans are naturally inclined to worship and rely on a higher power, especially in times of distress. The author cites the Qur'anic verse (29:65) as evidence that even polytheists turn to God sincerely when in danger. Third, the human soul innately distinguishes between high and low, preferring the noble and good while detesting the elevation of the base. This leads to an innate sense of justice and moral valuation. Fourth, humans naturally accept good and reject evil when known. Finally, love of comfort and freedom are mentioned as examples. The passage thus establishes that certain universal human tendencies are part of the original creation, providing a basis for epistemology and ethics.

Key Terms

التعبد

Checkpoint
What evidence does the author use to support the claim that worship is innate?
A) The existence of idols in ancient times.
B) The universal presence of religion and places of worship throughout history.
C) The Quranic story of Prophet Ibrahim.
D) The fact that all people love comfort.

Key Takeaway
Innate religiosity and moral discrimination are fixed aspects of human nature, indicating that belief in God and moral values are not mere conventions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a person who claims to be atheist but in a life-threatening situation cries out 'Oh God!'. How does the author's argument explain this behavior? Write a short response.
?
Observe a child who naturally distinguishes between fairness and unfairness. Relate this to the author's claim that the soul works to place everything in its proper position.

Manifestations of Fitra in Human Life
Author presents observable expressions of fitra.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain three manifestations of fitra as described in the passage.

Core Idea
Fitra is universally manifest in worship, moral discernment, and love of freedom.

The author argues that fitra is not merely a theoretical concept but is observable in human behavior across history. In this lesson, we explore the three key manifestations of innate human nature that the author highlights from the passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first manifestation: universal worship
Find the part of the passage that describes the universal inclination to worship and the historical evidence for religious practice. Note the Quranic verse (29:65) that illustrates turning to God in hardship.
2
Recognize the second manifestation: innate moral discrimination
Locate where the author says the soul differentiates between high and low, good and evil, and prefers truthfulness over falsehood. Understand that this is an inherent moral sense.
3
Understand the third manifestation: love of comfort and freedom
See the brief mention at the end of the first paragraph: 'love of comfort and love of freedom' as instances of fitra.
4
Reflect on the universality of these manifestations
Consider how these three manifestations, according to the author, are fixed throughout history and not subject to change, showing fitra's permanent and universal character.

Source Text

الكمال المطلق ومن مظاهر الفطرة الثابتة إلى مدار التاريخ التعبد وهذه حقيقة غير قابلة للتبديل أو التغيير فالإنسان قد خلق وخلق معه الإحساس بالحاجة إلى الركون إلى عقيدة ما والتاريخ يشهد ويؤكد على أن ما من عصر أو زمان أو مكان إلا وكان الناس فيه متدينون بدين ونحن اليوم نجد في كل مدينة أو قرية مركزاً للعبادة سواء كان هذا المركز معبداً للأوثان أو كنيسةً أو مسجداً ثم إن الإنسان مفطور على اللجوء إلى ربه تبارك وتعالى عند الشدائد فإذا ما وقع الإنسان أي إنسان حتى الكافر الملحد في شدة أو أحدق به خطر فإن الخيالات والأوهام تتطاير من ذهنه ويبقى ما فطر عليه ليصيح بأعلى صوته ومن قرارة نفسه وعميق قلبه منادياً ربه ليفرج كربته وهمه ويلجأ إليه وحده دون سواه وصدق الله تعالى إذ يقول فَإِذَا رَكَبُوا فِي الْفُلْكِ دَعَوُا اللهَ فَلَمَّا نَجَاهُمْ إِلَى الْبَرِّ إِذَا هُمْ يُشْرِكُونَ ومن مظاهر الفطرة ان النفس الإنسانية لا تساوي بين العالي والسافل والشريف والوضيع فإن من طبعها التفريق بينهما وتفضيل العالي والشريف والخير على السافل والوضيع والشرير وتنفر غاية النفور من ترفع الأراذل وخفض الأفاضل إن النفس تعمل على اعلاء قيم الصدق والأمانة وإسفال قيم الكذب والخيانة وترى العدل كل العدل أن ينزل كل شيء منزلته ومن مظاهر الفطرة ان الانسان يقبل الخير حين يعلم بأنه خير ويرفض الشر حين يعلم بأنه شر ومن مصاديق الفطرة عشق الراحة وعشق الحرية سمات الفطرة نظرية المعرفة بين القرآن والفلسفة 1) انها عامة مشتركة لجميع الناس 2) انها ثابتة خالدة في صميم تكوين المخلوق منذ خلقه حتى موته لا يختلف مسيرهم ولا يدعو آخرهم إلا إلى ما دعا إليه أولهم وإن اختلفت دعوتهم بالإجمال والتفصيل بحسب اختلاف أعصار الإنسانية تكاملا ورقيا 3) انها تشمل الجانب الروحي والجانب المادي 4) هي متساوية عند جميع الناس قال تعالى كَانَ النَّاسُ أُمَّةً وَاحِدَةً والمراد فيها بالإنسان الفطري الإنسان الساذج الذي يعيش على الفطرة الإنسانية الذي لم تفسده الأوهام الفكرية والأهواء النفسانية وهذا دليل على سلامة الفطرة الخلقية الاولى 5) ان المعلومات الفطرية سابقة للعلم وهي اكثر اصالة منه وهي من الآية التي جاءت في أول البحث وَاللهُ أَخْرَجَكُمْ مِنْ بُطُونِ أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ لا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئًا مستثناة 6) الفطرة حالة استعداد لا تعني الإجبار وسلب الإختيار ويهتف له بما ينفعه وما يضره في حياته
Absolute perfection. Among the manifestations of innate nature fixed throughout the course of history is worship. This is a truth not subject to alteration or change. For man was created, and with him was created the feeling of need to lean towards some creed. History bears witness and confirms that there was no era, time, or place except that the people in it were religious with a religion. Today we find in every city or village a place of worship, whether this place is a temple of idols, a church, or a mosque. Then, man is innately disposed to resort to his Lord, Blessed and Exalted, during hardships. So when any man, even an atheist disbeliever, falls into distress or danger surrounds him, illusions and fantasies fly from his mind, and what he was created upon remains so that he cries out with his loudest voice, from the depth of his soul and the core of his heart, calling upon his Lord to relieve his distress and worry, and he resorts to Him alone without any other. And Allah Almighty spoke truthfully when He said: 'So when they board a ship, they supplicate Allah, sincere to Him in religion, but when He delivers them to the land, at once they associate others with Him.' And among the manifestations of innate nature is that the human soul does not equate the high and the low, the noble and the base. For it is in its nature to differentiate between them and to prefer the high, the noble, and the good over the low, the base, and the evil, and it is extremely repulsed by the elevation of the vile and the lowering of the virtuous. The soul works to elevate the values of truthfulness and trustworthiness and to lower the values of lying and betrayal, and it sees justice, all justice, as giving everything its proper place. And among the manifestations of innate nature is that man accepts good when he knows it is good and rejects evil when he knows it is evil. And among the instances of innate nature is the love of comfort and the love of freedom. Characteristics of innate nature: Theory of Knowledge between the Quran and Philosophy. 1) It is general and common to all people. 2) It is constant and eternal in the core of the creature's constitution from his creation until his death: 'their path does not differ, nor does the last of them call except to what the first of them called to, even if their calls differ in generality and detail according to the difference of human eras in development and progress.' 3) It encompasses the spiritual side and the material side. 4) It is equal among all people. Allah Almighty said: 'The people were one nation.' What is meant by 'fitri man' is the naive man who lives on human innate nature, whom intellectual illusions and psychological whims have not corrupted. This is evidence of the soundness of the original created innate nature. 5) Innate information precedes knowledge and is more original than it. This is from the verse that came at the beginning of the research: 'And Allah brought you out from the wombs of your mothers not knowing anything, except that which He taught you.' 6) Innate nature is a state of readiness; it does not mean compulsion and removal of choice, and it calls out to him with what benefits him and what harms him in his life.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of fitra (innate human nature) and lists its key characteristics. The author begins by asserting that the inclination to worship is a fixed manifestation of fitra throughout history, citing the universal presence of religious practice and the human tendency to turn to God in times of crisis, even among atheists. This is supported by Quran 29:65. Then, other manifestations are described: the innate moral discrimination between high and low, good and evil, the preference for truthfulness over falsehood, and the love of comfort and freedom. The second part enumerates six characteristics of fitra: (1) universality – it is common to all humans; (2) permanence – it is inherent from birth to death, with the idea that all prophets called to the same essentials despite differences in details; (3) comprehensiveness – covering spiritual and material aspects; (4) equality – all humans share it initially, as in Quran 2:213, and the 'fitri man' is the uncorrupted natural person; (5) primacy – innate knowledge precedes acquired knowledge and is more fundamental, referencing Quran 16:78 about being born without knowledge; (6) non-coercive – fitra is a preparedness, not a determinism, and it guides towards benefit and harm. The author treats fitra as an epistemological foundation, aligning with Quranic verses to argue that basic moral and theological truths are ingrained in humans. The discussion is theological-epistemological, not a logical proof.

الفطرة
المعلومات الفطرية

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Six Characteristics of Innate Nature (Fitra)
Author enumerates the six characteristics of fitra.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the six characteristics of fitra as enumerated in the passage.

Core Idea
Fitra is universal, permanent, comprehensive, equal, prior to knowledge, and non-coercive.

After describing the manifestations, the author provides a systematic list of six characteristics that define fitra. These characteristics establish fitra as a stable, universal, and non-deterministic foundation for human nature and knowledge.

Guided Path
1
List the six characteristics from the passage
Read the numbered list in the Arabic text (1-6). Summarize each in your own words: (1) general/common, (2) constant/eternal, (3) encompasses spiritual and material, (4) equal among all people, (5) innate knowledge precedes acquired knowledge, (6) state of readiness, not compulsion.
2
Identify supporting evidence for each
For each characteristic, note the Quranic verse or reasoning the author provides. For example, characteristic 2 is supported by the idea that all prophets called to the same essentials; characteristic 4 uses Quran 2:213; characteristic 5 uses Quran 16:78.
3
Distinguish between descriptive and epistemological characteristics
Group the characteristics: 1,2,3,4 describe the scope and nature of fitra (universal, permanent, comprehensive, equal), while 5 and 6 deal with its epistemological and volitional aspects (primacy of innate knowledge, non-coercive readiness).
4
Reflect on the significance of characteristic 5
Pay special attention to the claim that innate information precedes acquired knowledge and is more original. The author cites Quran 16:78 to argue that humans are born without knowledge but have a innate capacity that is prior to learning.
The word 'مستثناة' in the Arabic may be a copyist error; it likely refers to 'except that which He taught you' as an exception.

الكمال المطلق ومن مظاهر الفطرة الثابتة إلى مدار التاريخ التعبد وهذه حقيقة غير قابلة للتبديل أو التغيير فالإنسان قد خلق وخلق معه الإحساس بالحاجة إلى الركون إلى عقيدة ما والتاريخ يشهد ويؤكد على أن ما من عصر أو زمان أو مكان إلا وكان الناس فيه متدينون بدين ونحن اليوم نجد في كل مدينة أو قرية مركزاً للعبادة سواء كان هذا المركز معبداً للأوثان أو كنيسةً أو مسجداً ثم إن الإنسان مفطور على اللجوء إلى ربه تبارك وتعالى عند الشدائد فإذا ما وقع الإنسان أي إنسان حتى الكافر الملحد في شدة أو أحدق به خطر فإن الخيالات والأوهام تتطاير من ذهنه ويبقى ما فطر عليه ليصيح بأعلى صوته ومن قرارة نفسه وعميق قلبه منادياً ربه ليفرج كربته وهمه ويلجأ إليه وحده دون سواه وصدق الله تعالى إذ يقول فَإِذَا رَكَبُوا فِي الْفُلْكِ دَعَوُا اللهَ فَلَمَّا نَجَاهُمْ إِلَى الْبَرِّ إِذَا هُمْ يُشْرِكُونَ ومن مظاهر الفطرة ان النفس الإنسانية لا تساوي بين العالي والسافل والشريف والوضيع فإن من طبعها التفريق بينهما وتفضيل العالي والشريف والخير على السافل والوضيع والشرير وتنفر غاية النفور من ترفع الأراذل وخفض الأفاضل إن النفس تعمل على اعلاء قيم الصدق والأمانة وإسفال قيم الكذب والخيانة وترى العدل كل العدل أن ينزل كل شيء منزلته ومن مظاهر الفطرة ان الانسان يقبل الخير حين يعلم بأنه خير ويرفض الشر حين يعلم بأنه شر ومن مصاديق الفطرة عشق الراحة وعشق الحرية سمات الفطرة نظرية المعرفة بين القرآن والفلسفة 1) انها عامة مشتركة لجميع الناس 2) انها ثابتة خالدة في صميم تكوين المخلوق منذ خلقه حتى موته لا يختلف مسيرهم ولا يدعو آخرهم إلا إلى ما دعا إليه أولهم وإن اختلفت دعوتهم بالإجمال والتفصيل بحسب اختلاف أعصار الإنسانية تكاملا ورقيا 3) انها تشمل الجانب الروحي والجانب المادي 4) هي متساوية عند جميع الناس قال تعالى كَانَ النَّاسُ أُمَّةً وَاحِدَةً والمراد فيها بالإنسان الفطري الإنسان الساذج الذي يعيش على الفطرة الإنسانية الذي لم تفسده الأوهام الفكرية والأهواء النفسانية وهذا دليل على سلامة الفطرة الخلقية الاولى 5) ان المعلومات الفطرية سابقة للعلم وهي اكثر اصالة منه وهي من الآية التي جاءت في أول البحث وَاللهُ أَخْرَجَكُمْ مِنْ بُطُونِ أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ لا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئًا مستثناة 6) الفطرة حالة استعداد لا تعني الإجبار وسلب الإختيار ويهتف له بما ينفعه وما يضره في حياته
Absolute perfection. Among the manifestations of innate nature fixed throughout the course of history is worship. This is a truth not subject to alteration or change. For man was created, and with him was created the feeling of need to lean towards some creed. History bears witness and confirms that there was no era, time, or place except that the people in it were religious with a religion. Today we find in every city or village a place of worship, whether this place is a temple of idols, a church, or a mosque. Then, man is innately disposed to resort to his Lord, Blessed and Exalted, during hardships. So when any man, even an atheist disbeliever, falls into distress or danger surrounds him, illusions and fantasies fly from his mind, and what he was created upon remains so that he cries out with his loudest voice, from the depth of his soul and the core of his heart, calling upon his Lord to relieve his distress and worry, and he resorts to Him alone without any other. And Allah Almighty spoke truthfully when He said: 'So when they board a ship, they supplicate Allah, sincere to Him in religion, but when He delivers them to the land, at once they associate others with Him.' And among the manifestations of innate nature is that the human soul does not equate the high and the low, the noble and the base. For it is in its nature to differentiate between them and to prefer the high, the noble, and the good over the low, the base, and the evil, and it is extremely repulsed by the elevation of the vile and the lowering of the virtuous. The soul works to elevate the values of truthfulness and trustworthiness and to lower the values of lying and betrayal, and it sees justice, all justice, as giving everything its proper place. And among the manifestations of innate nature is that man accepts good when he knows it is good and rejects evil when he knows it is evil. And among the instances of innate nature is the love of comfort and the love of freedom. Characteristics of innate nature: Theory of Knowledge between the Quran and Philosophy. 1) It is general and common to all people. 2) It is constant and eternal in the core of the creature's constitution from his creation until his death: 'their path does not differ, nor does the last of them call except to what the first of them called to, even if their calls differ in generality and detail according to the difference of human eras in development and progress.' 3) It encompasses the spiritual side and the material side. 4) It is equal among all people. Allah Almighty said: 'The people were one nation.' What is meant by 'fitri man' is the naive man who lives on human innate nature, whom intellectual illusions and psychological whims have not corrupted. This is evidence of the soundness of the original created innate nature. 5) Innate information precedes knowledge and is more original than it. This is from the verse that came at the beginning of the research: 'And Allah brought you out from the wombs of your mothers not knowing anything, except that which He taught you.' 6) Innate nature is a state of readiness; it does not mean compulsion and removal of choice, and it calls out to him with what benefits him and what harms him in his life.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of fitra (innate human nature) and lists its key characteristics. The author begins by asserting that the inclination to worship is a fixed manifestation of fitra throughout history, citing the universal presence of religious practice and the human tendency to turn to God in times of crisis, even among atheists. This is supported by Quran 29:65. Then, other manifestations are described: the innate moral discrimination between high and low, good and evil, the preference for truthfulness over falsehood, and the love of comfort and freedom. The second part enumerates six characteristics of fitra: (1) universality – it is common to all humans; (2) permanence – it is inherent from birth to death, with the idea that all prophets called to the same essentials despite differences in details; (3) comprehensiveness – covering spiritual and material aspects; (4) equality – all humans share it initially, as in Quran 2:213, and the 'fitri man' is the uncorrupted natural person; (5) primacy – innate knowledge precedes acquired knowledge and is more fundamental, referencing Quran 16:78 about being born without knowledge; (6) non-coercive – fitra is a preparedness, not a determinism, and it guides towards benefit and harm. The author treats fitra as an epistemological foundation, aligning with Quranic verses to argue that basic moral and theological truths are ingrained in humans. The discussion is theological-epistemological, not a logical proof.

Key Terms
الفطرة
المعلومات الفطرية

C) Innate information precedes acquired knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The six characteristics of fitra establish it as a universal, primordial, and non-deterministic foundation for human knowledge and morality.

The Logical Argument for Fitra's Immutability
Author argues that fitra does not change, only weakens due to external factors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the author's argument for the immutability of fitra and identify the types of evidence used.

Core Idea
Fitra is fixed in creation; what changes is its expression, not its essence.

In this passage, the author tackles a crucial question: does the innate human disposition (fitra) change? This is not merely a theological curiosity — it affects how we understand human accountability and the role of education. The author employs both empirical observation and rational proof, alongside revealed texts, to defend the proposition that fitra itself is immutable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question
The passage begins with an explicit question: 'Does fitra change?' (هل تتغير الفطرة). Note this as the starting point of the inquiry.
2
Find the claim
The author answers clearly: fitra does not change. The core claim is that fitra is fixed (ثابتة) in the core of creation.
3
Locate the evidence
The author cites empirical experiences (التجارب) and rational proofs (البراهين العقلية). Then he references the Quran (30:30) and a hadith. Identify each as a distinct type of evidence.
Rational proofs establish the original principle of soundness; texts confirm the fitra.
4
Analyze the causal relationship
The author explains that fitra is affected (تتأثر) and weakened (تضعف) but not changed in essence. External factors like upbringing and environment influence its expression, not its substance.
Disease and deviation are accidental (عارضان) and treatable, not original.
5
Assess the role of education
The passage concludes that education and guidance preserve fitra. This implies that fitra remains intact but can be overshadowed; active measures are needed to maintain its uprightness.
The hadith about parents making the child Jewish etc. shows external influence, not a change in fitra itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هل تتغير الفطرة؟ سؤال لابد من طرحه ولاجل الاجابة الصحيحة نقول : دلت التجارب والبراهين العقلية على أن الأصل الأولي في الخليقة هو السلامة وأن المرض والانحراف أمران يعرضان على المزاج ويزولان بالمداواة والمعالجة، وليس هذا الأصل مختصاً بالسلامة من حيث العيوب الجسمانية، بل الأصل هو الطهارة الأقذار والأدران المعنوية) فقد خلق الإنسان على الفطرة النقية السليمة من الشرك والعصيان التي أشار إليها القرآن الكريم بقوله: {فطرة الله التي فطر الناس عليها} ان الفطرة لا تتغير لانها ثابتة في صميم الخلقة وانما تتاثر وتضعف لعوامل واسباب منها سوء التربية وفساد البيئة والعناد واللجاج (أن) تربية الإنسان والأجواء التي ينشأ فيها قد تلوث صفاء فطرته ونقاء وجدانه و للتربية أهمية في تنمية الفطرة وابعاد خطر شياطين الإنس في تدنيسها وحرفها إلى الضلال والشرك فإن العبرة من ذلك كله تكون بأن يعمل المسلمون أفرادا وجماعات وفي كل المجالات المختصة بالتعليم والتربية والتوجيه في المحافظة على الفطرة القويمة التي حباهم الله بها وخاصة لدى الناشئة قال النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم ) يولد الولد على الفطرة ثم يكون أبواه هما اللذان يهودانه أو ينصرانه أو يمجسانه كما تُنتج البهيمة بهيمة
Does fitra change? A question that must be asked. For the correct answer we say: Experiences and rational proofs have indicated that the original principle in creation is soundness, and that disease and deviation are two matters that occur to the temperament and disappear with treatment. And this principle is not specific to soundness from physical defects; rather, the origin is purity from moral filth and stains. Thus, man was created upon the pure fitra, free from polytheism and disobedience, which the Holy Quran referred to in His saying: 'The fitra of Allah upon which He created mankind.' Fitra does not change because it is fixed in the core of creation; rather, it is affected and weakened by factors and causes, including poor upbringing, corrupt environment, and stubbornness. (That) a person's upbringing and the atmospheres in which he grows up may pollute the clarity of his fitra and the purity of his conscience. And education has importance in developing fitra and warding off the danger of human devils in defiling it and diverting it to error and polytheism. The lesson from all this is that Muslims individually and collectively, and in all fields related to education, upbringing, and guidance, should preserve the upright fitra that Allah has gifted them, especially among the youth. The Prophet said: Every child is born upon fitra, then his parents make him a Jew, Christian, or Magian, just as the animal gives birth to an animal.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage addresses the question of whether fitra can change. The author begins by affirming the question's importance. The answer draws on both empirical experiences (tajārib) and rational proofs (barāhīn 'aqliyya) to establish that the original state of creation (al-aṣl al-awwalī) is soundness (salāma). Disease and deviation are accidental (ārīḍān) and treatable. This principle applies not only to physical health but also to moral purity. The author then cites Quran 30:30 to support that humans are created upon a pure fitra free from shirk and disobedience. The core claim is that fitra itself does not change—it is fixed in the essence of creation. However, it can be affected (tata'aththar) and weakened (tad'uf) by external factors such as poor upbringing, corrupt environment, and obstinacy. The author stresses the critical role of education (tarbiya) in preserving and nurturing fitra, especially in youth. The Prophetic hadith (born upon fitra, then parents alter it) is presented as evidence that while fitra is innate, external influences can distort its expression. The passage concludes with an exhortation for Muslims to actively safeguard fitra through education and guidance.

Key Terms
الفطرة
السلامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It changes completely.
B) It is affected and weakened.
C) It disappears.
D) It becomes corrupt.

Key Takeaway
Fitra is immutable in its essence; only its expression is susceptible to external influences.

?

Fitrah: The Unchangeable Innate Disposition and the Nature of Deviation
Author defines fitrah as innate disposition and explains deviation as misuse, not alteration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why deviation from fitrah is a misuse rather than an alteration, using the author's examples and Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Fitrah is fixed; deviation is misuse, not change.

This passage explores the concept of fitrah—the innate disposition upon which Allah created humanity—and clarifies a critical distinction: deviation from fitrah's rulings does not mean fitrah itself changes. The author uses vivid analogies and Quranic verses to show that fitrah remains intact even when people act contrary to it. Understanding this distinction is essential for sound theological reasoning about human nature and moral responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of fitrah
Find how the author defines fitrah at the start. Note that it is 'the beginning of creation' and includes physical, mental, and spiritual dimensions.
2
Extract the Quranic basis
Locate the verse (30:30) and note what it claims about fitrah: it is the religion of Allah with no change.
3
Analyze the deviation vs. alteration distinction
The author gives two analogies: the archer missing the target (misuse, not change of the bow's function) and tools like knives used crookedly (they still cut, but not as intended). What do these analogies illustrate about deviation?
4
Examine the extreme deviation example
Consider the author's example of using a saw for sewing (impossible because it would nullify the tool's purpose). How does this support the idea that fitrah itself cannot be changed?
5
Apply to real-world deviations
The author mentions homosexuality and incest. Explain how these are 'reversals' or 'misuse' of fitrah, not evidence that fitrah is altered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفطرة ها هنا ابتداء الخلق ويتبين من خلال الحديث الشريف ومن خلال الوقائع الثابتة في دنيا الحياة أن الولد يتأثر بأبويه من ناحية الجسم والبنية ومن ناحية العقل والذكاء ومن ناحية الفكر والعقيدة قليلاً أو كثيرًا سلباً أو إيجاباً ولذلك نجد كل مولود يعتنق معتقد ومذهب مربيه فترى اليهودي يدافع عن اليهودية ويرى في عزير أنه (الله)، وينطبق ذلك أيضاً على النصارى الذين يقولون ان عيسى ابن الله ومن هذا التصور يمكننا القول ان الانسان لوتربى تربية طبيعية سليمة لاختار الاسلام والتوحيد بلا شك لان الشرائع الإلهية ثم الدواعي النفسانية الموافقة لها كلها فطرية فالتساؤل عن الله والبحث عن مقاصده أمر تكويني ينبع من الأعماق دون قصد أو إرادة فاذا صادف قلوبا صافية فارغة من الخبث تمكن منها تمكنا شديدا والرسل بعثوا بتكميل الفطرة وتقريرها لا بتحويل الفطرة وتغييرها أن الدين وأصول فروعه الكلية مركوزة في النفس البشرية وهو شيء أشار إليه قوله سبحانه (فَأَقِمْ وَجْهَكَ لِلدِّينِ حَنِيفاً فِطْرَتَ اللهِ الَّتِي فَطَرَ النَّاسَ عَلَيْهَا لا تبْدِيلَ لِخَلْقِ الله ذلكَ الدِّينُ القَيْمُ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَ النَّاسِ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ) ان الذي فطر عليه البشر هو الدين بمعناه الوسيع الشامل للعقيدة والأخلاق والقيم والسجايا أي العقيدة السليمة وبالتالي لاتعارض عندما نقول فطرة الله بمعنى الدين الإسلام أو التوحيد ) وهناك نوعان من التصرف الانساني خارج قوانين الفطرة وهما الانحراف والسمو ( وأما الانحراف المشهود عن أحكام الفطرة فليس إبطالا لحكمها بل استعمالا لها في غير ما ينبغي له من نحو الاستعمال مثال : ربما يتفق إن الرامي لا يصيب الهدف في رميته فإن آلة الرمي و سائر شرائطه موضوعة بالطبع للإصابة إلا أن الاستعمال يوقعها في الخطأ والسكاكين والمناشير والمثاقب والإبر وأمثالها إذا عبئت في الماكينات تعبئة معوجة تعمل عملها الذي فطرت عليه بعينه من قطع أو نشر أو ثقب و غير ذلك لكن لا على الوجه المقصود و أما الانحراف عن العمل الفطري كأن يخاط بنشر المنشار، بأن يعوض المنشار فعل الإبرة من فعل نفسه فيضع الخياطة موضع النشر فمن المحال ذلك أن الفطرة لن تبطل البتة وإنما يخطأ الإنسان في كيفية استعمالها ) فهو مخلوق على احسن مايرام وفي أجمل تقويم أي في أحسن هيئة قال تبارك وتعالى (لَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا الْإِنْسَانَ فِي أحسن تقويم . ثم رَدَدْنَاهُ أَسْفَلَ سَافِلِينَ . إِلَّا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ فَلَهُمْ أَجْرٌ غَيْرُ مَمْنُون فاللوطية مثلا عكسوا فطرة الله التي فطر عليها الرجال وقلبوا الطبيعة التي ركبها الله في الرجال، وهي شهوة النساء دون الذكور فقلبوا الأمر وعكسوا الفطرة والطبيعة والخروج على حكم الفطرة غير تبديل الفطرة. فالفطرة لا تبدل لأنها حجة بذاتها عند الإنسان) ومن نماذج هذا الانحراف مثلا مباشرة الاخ للاخت مثلا ويمكن أن نمثل فطرة الله التي فطر الناس عليها بأنها جيناً وراثياً لا يمكن تعديله في مختبر علمي جين وراثي من الممكن ان بصاب بالمرض وفي حالة عمل الغريزة الجنسية في مرحلة أعلى
And the fitrah here is the beginning of creation, and it becomes clear through the noble hadith and through the established facts in the life of this world that the child is influenced by his parents in terms of body and structure, and in terms of mind and intelligence, and in terms of thought and belief, little or much, negatively or positively. Therefore we find every newborn adopts the belief and madhhab of his educator. So you see the Jew defending Judaism and considering 'Uzayr as (Allah), and the same applies to the Christians who say that Jesus is the son of Allah. From this conception we can say that if a human were raised with a sound natural upbringing, he would choose Islam and tawhid without doubt, because the divine laws and the psychological motives that agree with them are all fitri. So questioning about Allah and searching for His purposes is a constitutive matter that springs from the depths without intention or will. If it encounters pure hearts empty of malice, it takes hold of them strongly. And the messengers were sent to complete the fitrah and establish it, not to transform the fitrah and change it. Indeed, the religion and the universal principles of its branches are ingrained in the human soul, and this is something indicated by His saying, the Exalted: 'So set your face to the religion, inclining to truth, [adhere to] the fitrah of Allah upon which He has created [all] people. No change should there be in the creation of Allah. That is the correct religion, but most people do not know.' That upon which humans are created is the religion in its broad sense that includes creed, morals, values, and natural dispositions, i.e., the sound creed. Hence there is no contradiction when we say 'the fitrah of Allah' meaning the religion of Islam or tawhid. And there are two types of human behavior outside the laws of fitrah: deviation and elevation. As for the observed deviation from the rulings of fitrah, it is not an invalidation of its ruling but rather a use of it in an inappropriate manner, like the example: perhaps it happens that an archer does not hit the target in his shot, for the shooting apparatus and all its conditions are naturally set for hitting, but use causes it to fall into error. And knives, saws, drills, needles, and the like, if they are loaded in machines in a crooked manner, they perform the very function they were created for, such as cutting, sawing, drilling, etc., but not in the intended way. As for deviation from the fitri function, such as sewing with a saw, i.e., substituting the saw for the needle's own action, placing sewing in the place of sawing—that is impossible because the fitrah will never be nullified; rather, man errs in how he uses it. So he is created in the best state and in the most beautiful form, i.e., in the best constitution. He said, Blessed and Exalted: 'We have certainly created man in the best of stature; then We return him to the lowest of the low, except for those who believe and do righteous deeds, for they will have a reward uninterrupted.' For example, homosexuals reversed the fitrah of Allah upon which He created men, and overturned the nature that Allah instilled in men, which is desire for women, not males. So they inverted the matter and reversed the fitrah and nature. And going against the ruling of fitrah is not changing the fitrah. For fitrah is not changed because it is a proof in itself for man. And examples of this deviation include a brother's direct [sexual] approach to his sister. And we can represent the fitrah of Allah upon which He created people as a genetic gene that cannot be modified in a scientific laboratory—a genetic gene that can become diseased, and in the case of the sexual instinct operating at a higher stage...
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological explanation of the concept of fitrah (innate disposition) and the nature of deviation from it. The author begins by establishing that fitrah is the original creation of humans, and that a child is influenced by parents in body, mind, and belief. This influence explains why people adopt the religion of their upbringing, but the author argues that if a person were raised naturally, he would choose Islam and tawhid because divine laws and psychological motives are all fitri (innate). The desire to know Allah is constitutive and emerges spontaneously. Prophets came to complete and establish the fitrah, not to change it. The author then cites the Quranic verse (30:30) to support that religion is ingrained in human nature. He then distinguishes two types of behavior outside the laws of fitrah: deviation (inhiraf) and elevation (sumuww). He clarifies that deviation is not an abolition of fitrah but a misuse—like an archer missing the target because of incorrect use, or tools like knives and saws that function as designed but not as intended if loaded crookedly. A deeper deviation would be using a tool for a completely different function, e.g., sewing with a saw, which is impossible because it nullifies the tool's purpose. Fitrah itself never changes; only its application can be erroneous. The author then uses the example of homosexuality as a reversal of fitrah, noting that going against the ruling of fitrah is not the same as changing fitrah itself. He further illustrates with incest as another deviation. Finally, he metaphorically describes fitrah as a genetic gene that cannot be altered in a lab but can become diseased. The overall message is that fitrah is a fixed, inherent disposition that cannot be changed, but humans can deviate by misusing it.

Key Terms
الفطرة
الانحراف
السمو

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between deviation and fitrah?
A) Deviation permanently alters the fitrah.
B) Deviation is a misuse of fitrah, not a change.
C) Deviation occurs only in non-religious contexts.
D) Fitrah can be completely eradicated by deviation.

Key Takeaway
Fitrah is the unchangeable innate disposition; deviation is misuse of that disposition, not its alteration.

Quranic Epistemology: Fitra, Sibgha, and Mithaq
Author defines fitra, sibgha, and mithaq as Quranic innate dispositions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Quranic concepts of fitra, sibgha, and mithaq from Descartes' theory of innate ideas, and identify their definitions as latent powers in human nature.

Core Idea
Fitra, sibgha, and mithaq are three complementary Quranic concepts describing man's innate disposition to know God.

In this passage, the author explores three key Quranic terms that relate to human nature and knowledge: fitra, sibgha, and mithaq. These are not merely theological abstractions but are presented as latent powers within every human being. Understanding these concepts is essential for grasping the Islamic epistemological framework, which differs fundamentally from Western theories like Descartes' innate ideas.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definitions
Find the author's one-sentence definitions of fitra, sibgha, and mithaq. Note how each is described as a 'latent power' or 'original feeling'.
Fitra: latent power to discover truth; Sibgha: latent power to show goodness; Mithaq: original feeling that God is Creator.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
What verses does the author cite for sibgha (Surah al-Baqarah 138) and mithaq (Surah al-A'raf 172)? How does the author interpret these verses?
Sibgha is explained as a permanent divine dye; mithaq as a primordial covenant embedded in human nature.
3
Compare the three concepts
Look for the author's statement that there is 'no contradiction, but integration, compatibility, and harmony.' How do these three concepts relate to each other?
They are complementary aspects of the same innate disposition.
4
Distinguish from Descartes
The author explicitly contrasts fitra with Descartes' innate ideas. What is the key difference according to the author?
Descartes: innate ideas in the mind; Quran: latent desires that emerge through contact with the external world.
5
Recognize the epistemological shift
Note that the author emphasizes that latent innate information is 'deeper, more stable, and more original than insights.' What does this imply about Islamic epistemology?
Knowledge is not merely rational but grounded in primordial human nature.

عبد الزهرة تركي الفتلاوي
(الفطرة) فاذا حادوا عن هذا كان بسقم تفكير أو قبح تقليد وأشهد الله هؤلاء الآدميين جميعا على انفسهم بأن الله واحد لاخالق ولا معبود سواه شهادة تعقل بعد روية وتفكير ولم تكن نتيجة كلام يقال فليس الحديث هنا عن ان الانسان بعد ان رأى نفسه فهم أن له الها بل الحديث هنا ان الله أرى نفسه للانسان في اعماق ذاته وفي هذا المعنى ورد قول الفيلسوف أمرسن (إن في مقدور الانسان أي أنسان أن يرى الله في اعماق قلبه وانه اذا أنصت الى ضميره بأذن مصغية واعية سمع صوت الله في دخيلة نفسه) وبعبارات موجزة ان الفطرة هي القوة الكامنة في ذات الانسان لاكتشاف الحق والحقيقة اما الصبغة فهي قوة كامنة تجعل الانسان يريد اظهار الجانب الخير على ذاته امام المجتمع . أما الميثاق فهو الشعور الاصيل في اعماق الانسان بأن الله هو الخالق يوجد تعارض بين مفاهيم الفطرة والصبغة والميثاق التي طرحها القرآن الكريم بل هناك تكامل وتوافق وانسجام ولابد من الاشارة الى ان موضوع الفطرة في القرآن الكريم لايمت بصلة لنظرية الافكار الفطرية التي طرحها دیکارت فهذه النظرية تقول بوجود أفكار في حين ان نظرية القرآن تتحدث عن رغبات كامنة في اعماق النفس البشرية ومن ثم تخرج الى الفعل من خلال التفتح التدريجي بعد الاتصال بالخارج عبر ادوات المعرفة. ان هذه الرغبات تتوزع في جميع ادوات المعرفة فالعين ترغب في رؤية المناظر الطبيعية والاذن ترغب في سماع النغمات الهادئة والقلب يعشق كل جميل والنفس ترغب في زيادة الثروة وهناك دراسات كاملة في علم النفس حول موضوع الرغبات الفطرية ان المعلومات الفطرية الكامنة أكثر عمقا وثباتا وأصالة من البصائر.
١ سورة البقرة الآية ۱۳۸
٢ المفردات في غريب القرآن الراغب الاصفهاني، مصدر سابق ص ۲۷۸

Theory of knowledge between the Quran and philosophy. The summit (organism?) is connected to the depths of innate nature (fitra), and it is possible for man to rise above the laws of fitra, as occurs when a man gives up part of his wealth for the poor or sacrifices himself for the public interest of society, etc. As mentioned in the Holy Quran, terms close to the concept of fitra include al-sibgha and al-mithaq, as in His saying (the dye of God, and who is better than God in dyeing? And we are His worshippers). (Al-sibgh is the source of sibgha, and al-sibgh is the dyed thing. Sibghat Allah refers to what God has created in people that distinguishes them from animals). Indeed, God has dyed us with this religion with a dye that appears on us as the dye appears on cloth and distinguishes it by its colors. That is a comparison to the original dye that dyes cloth so that it becomes from its origin impervious to erasure or destruction, indicating what God has created in people of natures that distinguish them from animals. The Christians, when a child was born to them, immersed him after the seventh day in baptismal water claiming that it was a sibgha. So God said (And who is better than God in dyeing?). And in the expression of mithaq, He said (And when your Lord took from the children of Adam from their backs their descendants and made them testify over themselves, 'Am I not your Lord?' They said, 'Yes, we testify' lest you say on the Day of Resurrection, 'Indeed we were unaware of this'). The discussion here is about humans in general and their stance on acknowledging lordship and taking the covenant, and that it is a creation and a root embedded in their nature by virtue of what God created for them of sound minds capable of thinking about everything God created. So humans, generation after generation, grow up on the religion of sound thinking. (Fitra) So if they deviate from this, it is due to flawed thinking or ugly imitation. And God made all these humans testify over themselves that God is one, no creator and no worshipped other than Him, a testimony of reason after consideration and reflection, and it was not the result of spoken words. So the discussion here is not about man after seeing himself understanding that he has a god, but rather God showed Himself to man in the depths of his essence. In this sense, the saying of the philosopher Emerson: 'It is within the power of any man to see God in the depths of his heart, and if he listens to his conscience with an attentive and conscious ear, he will hear God's voice in his inner self.' In brief terms, fitra is the latent power in man's essence to discover truth and reality. As for sibgha, it is a latent power that makes man want to show the good aspect of himself before society. As for mithaq, it is the original feeling in the depths of man that God is the Creator. There is no contradiction between the concepts of fitra, sibgha, and mithaq presented by the Holy Quran; rather there is integration, compatibility, and harmony. It must be pointed out that the topic of fitra in the Holy Quran is not related to the theory of innate ideas proposed by Descartes. That theory speaks of the existence of ideas, while Quranic theory speaks of latent desires in the depths of the human soul, then they come out into action through gradual opening after contact with the outside via the tools of knowledge. These desires are distributed among all the tools of knowledge: the eye desires to see natural scenes, the ear desires to hear calm melodies, the heart loves everything beautiful, and the soul desires to increase wealth. And there are complete studies in psychology on the topic of innate desires. Indeed, latent innate information is deeper, more stable, and more original than insights. (Footnotes: 1 Surah al-Baqarah verse 138; 2 Al-Mufradat fi Gharib al-Quran by al-Raghib al-Isfahani, previous source p. 278; 3 Surah al-A'raf verse 172; 1 God Reveals Himself in the Age of Science, group of scientists, translation by Abdul-Majid al-Damardash, Dar al-Tarbiya Baghdad 1988 p. 24)

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological exposition by the author defining three Quranic concepts: fitra (innate nature), sibgha (divine dye/baptism), and mithaq (primordial covenant). The author begins by noting that terms close to fitra appear in the Quran, namely sibgha and mithaq. The concept of sibgha is explained through the Quranic verse 'Sibghat Allah' (the dye of God), where the author interprets 'sibgha' metaphorically as a permanent dye that God has impressed upon humans, distinguishing them from animals. The author contrasts this with Christian baptism. Next, the mithaq is discussed with reference to the verse of the covenant (Surah al-A'raf 172), where God took a covenant from all descendants of Adam, making them testify that He is their Lord. This covenant is described as embedded in human nature. The author then summarizes: fitra is the latent power to discover truth, sibgha is the power to manifest goodness before society, and mithaq is the original feeling that God is the Creator. The author emphasizes that these concepts are not contradictory but complementary. Finally, the author distinguishes the Quranic notion of fitra from Descartes' theory of innate ideas, noting that Descartes speaks of innate ideas while the Quran speaks of latent desires that emerge through interaction with the external world. The passage concludes with an observation that innate latent information is deeper and more stable than insights.

Definition and Types of Revelation (al-Wahy)
Definition and expansion of revelation types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the different modes of revelation as described in the Quran and hadith, and identify which individuals are reported to have received revelation.

Core Idea
Revelation is a divine compass for all humanity, not limited to prophets.

This passage defines revelation as internal divine signals that guide human knowledge. It explains various modes of revelation to prophets through a hadith from Imam Baqir and provides Quranic examples of revelation to non-prophets. Understanding this helps clarify the epistemological foundation of Islamic knowledge and the role of divine communication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of revelation
Read the author's definition in the conclusion: 'الوحي إشارات داخلية ربانية كتوجيه البوصلة للاسهام في تكامل المعرفة البشرية'. What is its purpose?
2
List the modes of revelation to prophets
From the hadith of Imam Baqir, identify the five types: hearing sound like a chain, being informed in a dream, seeing, having it inscribed in the heart, and having it made to ring in the ear.
Each mode represents a different sensory or intuitive channel.
3
Identify Quranic examples of revelation to non-prophets
The author cites verses about the disciples of Jesus, the mother of Moses, Mary, and Asiya. What do these have in common? They are righteous individuals, not prophets.
This expands the typical understanding of revelation.
4
Analyse the shift in the concept
Compare the classical limitation of revelation to prophets with the author's extension. How does this affect the epistemological status of knowledge from these sources?
The shift is significant for Islamic epistemology.

معاينة كسماع موسى كلام الله أو بالالقاء في الروع كما في قول النبي محمد ( ص) ( ان روح القدس نفث في روعي) (الروع : الخلد واستعمل فيما القي فيه من الفزع كقوله عز وجل : فلما ذهب عن ابرهيم الروع) ان الوحي الى الانبياء في الحقيقة هو وحي الى عامة البشر بوساطة الانبياء وهناك وحي الى بعض الناس الصالحين كما هو شأن الحواريين اصحاب عيسى السلام قال تعالى (وَإِذْ أَوْحَيْتُ إِلَى الْحَوَارِيِّينَ أَنْ آمِنُوا بِي وَبِرَسُولِي) وأم موسى (وَأَوْحَيْنَا إِلَى أَمْ مُوسَى أَنْ أَرْضِعِيهِ فَإِذَا خِفْتِ عَلَيْهِ فَأَلْقِيهِ فِي الْيَمِّ)، والى مريم بنت عمران وآسيا بنت مزاحم التي قالت بعد ان جاءها الوحي (وَقَالَتِ امْرَأَةُ فرعون قرةً عَيْنٍ لِي وَلَكَ لَا تَقْتُلُوهُ عَسَى أَنْ يَنفَعَنَا أَو تَتَّخِذَهُ وَلَدًا وَهُمْ لَا يَشْعُرُونَ) والى آخرين غيرها ( وأوحينا إليهم فعلَ الْخَيْرَاتِ) روي عن زرارة عن أبي جعفر عليه السلام قال : الانبياء على خمسة أنواع منهم من يسمع الصوت مثل صوت السلسلة فيعلم ما عني به ومنهم ينبأ في منامه مثل يوسف وابراهيم ومنهم من يعاين ومنهم من ينكث في قلبه ويوقر في أذنه . الخلاصة : الوحي إشارات داخلية ربانية كتوجيه البوصلة للاسهام في تكامل المعرفة البشرية .
Seeing like Moses hearing the speech of Allah, or by inspiration into the heart, as in the saying of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him): 'The Holy Spirit breathed into my heart' (al-Raw': the heart, and used for what is cast into it of fright, as in His saying: 'When the fright departed from Abraham'). Indeed, revelation to the prophets is in reality a revelation to all people through the intermediary of the prophets. It is narrated from Zurara from Abu Ja'far (peace be upon him) said: The prophets are of five types: among them one who hears a sound like the sound of a chain and thus knows what is intended; among them one who is informed in his dream like Joseph and Abraham; among them one who sees; among them one who has it inscribed in his heart and made to ring in his ear. Conclusion: Revelation is internal divine signals, like directing a compass, to contribute to the integration of human knowledge.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage defines revelation as a form of divine communication that extends beyond the prophets to certain righteous individuals. The author begins by distinguishing different modes: sensory hearing like Moses, inspiration into the heart (as in the hadith), and then clarifies that revelation to prophets is ultimately for all humanity. Examples from the Quran include the disciples of Jesus, the mother of Moses, Mary, and Asiya. Then a hadith from Imam Baqir categorizes prophets into five types: those who hear a sound like a chain, those informed in dreams (like Joseph and Abraham), those who see, those who have it inscribed in the heart, and those who have it made to ring in the ear. The conclusion summarizes revelation as internal divine signals guiding human knowledge. The passage emphasizes the epistemological role of revelation in the Islamic tradition.

The Three Sequential Levels of Guidance
Author enumerates and classifies types of divine guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three sequential levels of divine guidance (hidaya) from the passage and explain why each is a prerequisite for the next.

Core Idea
Guidance is not monolithic: three levels build upon each other, starting with constitutive capacity.

The Quran mentions many types of guidance. In this passage, the author organizes them into a hierarchy. The most fundamental distinction is between constitutive guidance, path illumination, and conveyance to the goal. Understanding this sequence is crucial for appreciating how divine guidance operates in epistemology and taklif.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three levels
Find the three distinct types of guidance named in the passage: constitutive (takwiniyya), illumination of the path (inara al-tariq), and conveyance to the desired (isal ila al-matloob).
The Arabic terms appear after the discussion of negative guidance.
2
Understand the sequential relationship
The passage explicitly says the three are 'muratab' (sequential). Determine what each level enables and why the first is necessary for the second, and the second for the third.
The author states: whoever does not attain the first cannot attain the second, and obligation is not valid.
3
Relate to taklif
Constitutive guidance is the foundational capacity. Without it, a person is not morally obligated. This is a key theological point.
This concept is used in discussions of human responsibility before Allah.
4
Identify human limitation
The author notes that humans can only guide through supplication and teaching. Understand which level(s) this pertains to.
Humans cannot grant constitutive guidance; that is exclusively divine.

توبيخ وعقاب كما في قوله تعالى إِنْ اللَّهَ لَا يَهْدِي مَنْ هُوَ كَاذِبٌ كَفَّانَ إِنْ اللهَ لَا يَهْدِي الْقَوْمَ الظَّالِمِينَ) وهناك آيات عديدة جاءت في مقام نفي الهداية عن القوم ( الفاسقين ) و ( الظالمين) و(الكافرين) وهي كثيرة . ب : الايصال الى المطلوب في الآخرة : أي الهداية إلى الجنة أو الهداية الى النار قال تعالى (إِنَّ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ يَهْدِيهِمْ رَبَّهُم بِإِيمَانِهِم تَجْرِي مِن تَحْتِهِمُ الْأَنْهَارُ فِي جَنَّاتِ النعيم ( ۳ ) وقال أهل الجنة فيها الحمد لله الذي هدانا لهذا قال جل وعلا (وَالَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا في سبيل الله فَلَنْ يُضِلَّ أعْمَالَهُمْ . سيهديهم ويصلح بالهم ويدخلهم الجنة عرفها لهم سيهديهم لأنهم قتلوا في الجهاد فالهداية هنا ليست هداية الدنيا فإنما هي هداية الآخرة وقال تعالى عن أهل النار (احْشُرُوا) الَّذِينَ ظَلَمُوا وَأَزْوَاجَهُمْ وَمَا كَانُوا يَعْبُدُونَ . مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ فَاهَدُوهُمْ إِلَى صِرَاطِ الْجَحِيمِ وهذه الهدايات ( التكوينية ، إنارة الطريق ، الايصال الى المطلوب ) مترتبة فإن من لم تحصل له الاولى لا تحصل له الثانية بل لا يصح تكليفه ومن لم تحصل له الثانية لا تحصل له الثالثة ومن حصلت له الثالثة فقد حصلت لـه اللتان قبلهما والانسان لايقدر ان بهدي أحدا الا بالدعاء وتعريف الطرق. ونستنتج من خلال هذا البحث الموجز إن للهداية انواعا عديدة منها عامة لجميع الكائنات ومنها خاصة للنوع الانساني فقط ومنها ظاهرة كالكتب السماوية ومنها ضامرة كهداية الحواس وهناك هداية مواهب كنجدي الخير والشر ومنها هداية مكاسب كهداية المؤمنين وهناك هداية علمية كعلم الانسان ان مرضاة الله بالتوجه الى الكعبة وفي اداء الصلاة وهداية عملية أي الإرشاد لشعائر الحج وماهية حركات الصلاة . كما توجد هداية دائمة مثل هداية المنافع وهداية مؤقتة كهداية المعجزة وهداية الرؤيا المنامية الخلاصة: الهداية في نظرية القرآن مصدر للمعرفة وهي أشبه بالنور الذي يقود الانسان الى ما قرره الله سبحانه وإن كل معرفة لا تبلغ الكمال وستكون محتاجة الى الهداية
Rebuke and punishment as in His saying, 'Indeed, Allah does not guide one who is a liar, an ungrateful [sinner].' Indeed, Allah does not guide the wrongdoing people. And there are many verses that came in the context of denying guidance to the people (the defiantly disobedient), and (the wrongdoers), and (the disbelievers) — and they are many. B: Conveyance to the desired in the Hereafter: That is, guidance to Paradise or guidance to the Fire. He said, 'Indeed, those who have believed and done righteous deeds - their Lord will guide them because of their faith. Beneath them rivers flow in the Gardens of Pleasure.' And the people of Paradise said, 'Praise be to Allah, who has guided us to this.' He said, 'And those who are killed in the cause of Allah - He will never let their deeds be lost. He will guide them and amend their condition and admit them to Paradise, which He has made known to them. He will guide them because they were killed in jihad, so guidance here is not the guidance of this world; rather, it is the guidance of the Hereafter.' And He said about the people of the Fire, 'Gather together those who wronged and their kinds and what they used to worship besides Allah, and guide them to the path of Hellfire.' And these guidances (constitutive, illumination of the path, conveyance to the desired) are sequential: whoever does not attain the first does not attain the second; rather, his obligation is not valid. Whoever does not attain the second does not attain the third. And whoever attains the third has attained the two before it. And man cannot guide anyone except through supplication and defining the paths. And we conclude from this brief research that guidance has many types: some are general for all creatures, some are specific only to the human species, some are apparent like the heavenly books, some are hidden like the guidance of the senses. There is guidance of endowments like the guidance of good and evil, and guidance of acquisitions like the guidance of believers. There is scientific guidance like man's knowledge that pleasing Allah is by facing the Kaaba and performing prayer, and practical guidance i.e., guidance for the rites of Hajj and the nature of prayer movements. Also there is permanent guidance like the guidance of benefits, and temporary guidance like the guidance of miracles and the guidance of dream visions. Conclusion: Guidance in the Quranic theory is a source of knowledge, and it is like a light that leads man to what Allah has decreed. And every knowledge does not reach perfection and will be in need of guidance.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of the concept of 'guidance' (hidaya) from a Quranic perspective. The author begins by citing verses that negate guidance for certain types of people (liars, wrongdoers, disbelievers), establishing that guidance is not universal but contingent on divine will. He then distinguishes a second type: guidance to the desired outcome in the Hereafter — leading believers to Paradise and disbelievers to Hell. This is illustrated with Quranic verses about the reward of martyrs and the punishment of the wrongdoers. The author identifies three sequential levels of guidance: constitutive (takwiniyya, i.e., the initial capacity), illumination of the path (inara al-tariq, i.e., showing the way), and conveyance to the desired (isal ila al-matloob). These are ordered: without the first, the second cannot be attained; without the second, the third cannot be attained. Human beings can only guide by supplication and teaching, not by giving constitutive guidance. The author then lists many pairs of types: general vs. specific, apparent vs. hidden, endowment vs. acquisition, scientific vs. practical, permanent vs. temporary. The conclusion frames guidance as a source of knowledge similar to a light, without which knowledge remains incomplete. The passage is expository and descriptive, not argumentative in a logical sense.

Key Terms
الهداية
الهداية التكوينية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence of not having constitutive guidance (al-hidaya al-takwiniyya)?
A) One cannot be guided to Paradise
B) One's obligation (taklif) is not valid
C) One cannot receive the guidance of the senses
D) One is destined for Hellfire

Key Takeaway
The passage establishes a strict hierarchy: constitutive guidance enables capacity, path illumination shows the way, conveyance brings to the goal; each level depends on the previous.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take Quran 2:272: 'You are not responsible for their guidance, but Allah guides whom He wills.' Identify which of the three levels of guidance this might refer to and explain why.
?
Consider the case of a non-Muslim who has never heard of Islam. According to the author, does he have constitutive guidance? Does he have illumination of the path? Use the passage to answer.

The Many Pairs of Guidance Types
Author enumerates and classifies types of divine guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least six pairs of guidance types distinguished in the passage and classify a given instance of guidance into one of these pairs.

Core Idea
Guidance comes in many contrasting pairs: general/specific, apparent/hidden, endowment/acquisition, scientific/practical, permanent/temporary.

Beyond the three-level hierarchy, the passage enumerates multiple binary oppositions that classify guidance. These pairs show the richness of the concept in the Quran. They also help us locate different phenomena — from sensory perception to divine revelation — under the umbrella of hidaya.

Guided Path
1
Scan the passage for pairs
After the three levels, the author lists several pairs. Find them in the Arabic text: عامة / خاصة, ظاهرة / ضامرة, هداية مواهب / هداية مكاسب, علمية / عملية, دائمة / مؤقتة.
The pairs are introduced with 'منها ... ومنها'.
2
Match each type to an example
For each pair, the author gives or implies an example. For instance, 'apparent' includes heavenly books; 'hidden' includes guidance of the senses. Identify the examples for at least three pairs.
Some examples are explicit, others implicit (e.g., guidance of good and evil).
3
Understand the concluding statement
The author concludes that guidance is a source of knowledge like light. Relate this metaphor to the pairs: how do these diverse types all function as 'light'?
Consider that each type provides epistemic illumination in its domain.

Quranic Education as Divine Illumination
Author describes education as divine bestowal of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Quranic concept of ta'leem from conventional learning and identify its features as a form of 'ilm huduri.

Core Idea
Quranic education is divine direction, not information transfer.

In this passage, the author explores a profound Quranic perspective: education (ta'leem) is not merely the transmission of knowledge from teacher to student, but a divine bestowal — a direct illumination from Allah. This challenges an engineer's or doctor's default assumption that learning is purely intellectual acquisition. Let's unpack this concept and its implications for how we understand knowledge in the Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key Quranic verses cited
Scan the passage for the verses the author uses to support the concept of divine teaching. Note their content: 'And He teaches you what you did not know', 'And you have not been given of knowledge except a little', 'And that man has only what he strives for', and 'Read in the name of your Lord'.
These verses ground the author's thesis in revelation.
2
Extract the author's central claim about ta'leem
The author asserts that ta'leem in the Quran is a 'direction from Allah' (tasdid) and equates it with presential knowledge ('ilm huduri). Understand this as a direct, unmmediated bestowal of knowledge.
3
Contrast the two methods: conventional vs. presential
The author explicitly contrasts 'conventional mental transmission' (al-naql al-dhihni al-muta'arif) with 'presential knowledge' (fayd or ishraq). Recognize that the former is the usual teacher-student transfer, while the latter is divine emanation.
This is the core dichotomy of the passage.
4
Recognize 'ilm huduri as a technical term
The term 'ilm huduri (presential knowledge) is borrowed from Islamic philosophy, especially Suhrawardi. Realize that here it is applied to Quranic education, implying a direct awareness of God's teaching.
This term is not from classical Mantiq but from later epistemological discourse.
5
Reflect on the teleological purpose
The author says this education is 'a direction to develop life towards the better' and a 'divine honor and crowning of man's effort towards virtue and advancement'. Consider how this aligns with the Quranic view of human purpose.
Education here is not just informational but transformative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التعليم إن التعليم في مفهوم القرآن الكريم هو تسديد من الله للانسان ويعلمكم مَا لَمْ تَكُونُوا تَعْلَمُونَ ) ( ويعلمكم الله) تسديد لتطوير الحياة نحو الافضل (فالفيض المطلق الله العالم بكل شيء اعطى الى البشر الفيض القليل (وَمَا أوتِيتُمْ مِنَ الْعِلْم إلا قليلا وهذا التعليم لا ينال بالنقل الذهني المتعارف بل هو علم حضوري (فيض أو أشراق) وكذلك هو تكريم وتتويج الهي الجهد الانسان نحو الفضيلة والرقي وَأَنْ لَيْسَ لِلْإِنْسَانِ إِلَّا مَا سَعَى ويشير القرآن الكريم الى أرقى وسيلة للعلم وهي القراءة اقْرَأْ بِاسْمِ رَبِّكَ الَّذِي خَلَقَ خَلَقَ الْإِنْسَانَ مِنْ عَلَقٍ . اقْرَأْ وَرَبُّكَ الْأَكْرَمَ . الَّذِي عَلَّمَ بِالْقَلَم . عَلْمَ الْإِنْسَانَ
Education: Indeed, education in the concept of the Noble Quran is a direction from Allah to man: 'And He teaches you what you did not know' and 'And Allah teaches you' — a direction to develop life towards the better. So the absolute emanation of Allah, the Knower of everything, gave to humans the little emanation: 'And you have not been given of knowledge except a little.' And this education is not attained by conventional mental transmission; rather, it is presential knowledge (emanation or illumination). And likewise it is a divine honor and crowning of man's effort towards virtue and advancement: 'And that man has only what he strives for.' And the Noble Quran points to the highest means of knowledge, which is reading: 'Read in the name of your Lord who created, created man from a clot. Read, and your Lord is the Most Generous, who taught by the pen, taught man what he did not know.'
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage presents the Quranic conception of education (ta'leem) as fundamentally different from conventional learning. The author argues that education is essentially divine direction (tasdid) — God teaching humans what they did not know. This teaching is not achieved through mental transmission (al-naql al-dhihni al-muta'arif), i.e., the ordinary transfer of information from teacher to student. Instead, it is 'presential knowledge' ('ilm huduri) — a direct emanation (fayd) or illumination (ishraq) from God. This aligns with the verse 'And you have not been given of knowledge except a little,' indicating that human knowledge is a small overflow from the divine absolute emanation. The author further emphasizes that this education is a divine honor and crowning of human effort towards virtue and progress, citing 'And that man has only what he strives for.' Finally, the highest means of attaining knowledge is reading (iqra'), as commanded in the first revelation. Thus, the Quranic paradigm elevates education from mere informational transfer to an inspired, illuminative process.

Key Terms
التعليم (al-ta'leem): Divine teaching (tasdid) that imparts knowledge directly, as opposed to conventional mental transmission; it is a form of presential knowledge ('ilm huduri) or illumination (ishraq). [Note: In classical Mantiq, ta'leem is not a technical term; here it is used in an epistemological-sufi context.]
علم حضوري ('ilm huduri): Presential knowledge — direct awareness without intermediary, here equated with divine emanation or illumination. [Note: In Islamic philosophy (e.g., Suhrawardi), 'ilm huduri is a key concept; here it is applied to Quranic education.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is Quranic education (ta'leem) attained?
A) By memorizing and transmitting texts
B) By presential knowledge ('ilm huduri) through divine emanation
C) By logical deduction
D) By empirical observation

Key Takeaway
The passage positions Quranic education as a direct divine bestowal, not a product of human intellectual effort alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Read the passage again and identify two Quranic verses the author uses to support the idea that education is divine bestowal. Write down how each verse relates to the concept of 'ilm huduri.
?
Task 2: Compare this concept with the Aristotelian model of learning as described in classical Mantiq (knowledge from sense perception and deduction). In what ways are they compatible and incompatible?

Types of Divine Guidance (Hidaya) in Quranic Epistemology
Classification of divine guidance types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the types of divine guidance (hidaya) mentioned in the Quranic theory of knowledge and explain how they function as a source of knowledge.

Core Idea
Hidaya is a multifaceted divine light that guides all creation, yet perfect knowledge remains dependent on it.

This lesson explores the Quranic concept of hidaya as a primary source of knowledge. The passage classifies guidance into numerous categories, from general to specific, apparent to hidden. Understanding this taxonomy is crucial for grasping how divine guidance complements human reason in Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching claim
The passage states that hidaya is a source of knowledge like light. Note that it is not a single type but a spectrum.
2
List the types of hidaya
Scan the Arabic to find the classifications: general/specific, apparent/hidden, talents/acquisitions, scientific/practical, permanent/temporary.
The passage enumerates: هداية عامة, هداية خاصة, هداية ظاهرة, هداية ضامرة, هداية المواهب, هداية المكاسب, هداية علمية, هداية عملية, هداية دائمة, هداية مؤقتة.
3
Understand the function of each type
For example, scientific guidance (هداية علمية) pertains to knowing God's pleasure in worship; practical guidance (هداية عملية) pertains to rites like Hajj and prayer movements.
The passage gives examples: كعلم الانسان ان مرضاة الله بالتوجه الى الكعبة (scientific) and الإرشاد لشعائر الحج وماهية حركات الصلاة (practical).
4
Relate hidaya to knowledge perfection
The summary says every knowledge that does not reach perfection will be in need of guidance. Reflect on why even acquired knowledge requires divine guidance.
The passage: 'وإن كل معرفة لا تبلغ الكمال وستكون محتاجة الى الهداية.'

In this context, Alexis Carrel, a supporter of the idea of illumination and inspiration, says in his book 'Man, That Unknown': We must assert that scientific discoveries are not solely the product of human thought. For geniuses, in addition to possessing the ability for conscious reading and comprehending and investigating issues, they possess another power, which is the power of illumination and creative visualization. They recognized through illumination many things that were obscure and hidden from others, and they learned about relationships between things that apparently have no relation between them, and about many hidden unknown treasures, without analysis and reasoning.
